TL;DR President Trump declared near-total military victory in the five-week-old war against Iran (Operation Epic Fury), claiming the regime's military is "decimated" and its leadership dead, while warning of 2-3 more weeks of intense strikes to force a final nuclear deal. ...

TL;DR

President Trump declared near-total military victory in the five-week-old war against Iran (Operation Epic Fury), claiming the regime's military is "decimated" and its leadership dead, while warning of 2-3 more weeks of intense strikes to force a final nuclear deal.

Military Status and "Operation Epic Fury"

  • Operational Success: Trump claimed the U.S. has "obliterated" Iran’s Navy and Air Force, destroyed its missile and drone capabilities, and decimated the command and control of the Islamic Revolutionary Guard Corps (IRGC).
      • Scope of Strikes: Approximately 13,000 targets have been hit in 32 days of conflict.
      • Casualties: 13 U.S. service members have been killed in the operation; approximately 300 have been injured.
  • The "Stone Age" Timeline: The President signaled a final escalation, stating the military will hit Iran "extremely hard" over the next two to three weeks to "bring them back to the stone ages."
  • Ground Operations: Despite internal briefings on limited ground force options (such as seizing Kharg Island), the President did not announce a ground invasion, focusing instead on air and missile superiority.
  • Venezuela Mention: Trump noted a separate "quick, lethal" military action in Venezuela, referring to the country as a "joint venture partner" in oil production following a regime change.

Strategic Objectives and Regime Status

  • Nuclear Denial: The central stated goal remains ensuring Iran never acquires a nuclear weapon. Trump claimed previous strikes ("Operation Midnight Hammer") destroyed key facilities and that current operations have "checked the nuclear problem off the list."
  • Unintentional Regime Change: Trump asserted that while regime change was not the official goal, it has occurred because the original leadership is "all dead." He described the successor group as "less radical" and "more reasonable."
  • Future Targets: If negotiations fail, the President threatened to destroy Iran's entire electrical grid and its oil infrastructure, which has been intentionally spared thus far to allow for potential rebuilding.

Energy Security and the Strait of Hormuz

  • Gas Prices: Domestic gas prices have exceeded $4.00 per gallon. Trump dismissed this as a "short-term increase" caused by Iranian terror attacks on tankers, promising prices will "rapidly come back down" once the operation concludes.
  • U.S. Energy Independence: Trump emphasized that the U.S. is the world's top oil and gas producer and "imports almost no oil through the Hormuz strait," suggesting the U.S. no longer needs to secure the waterway for its own sake.
  • Ultimatum to Allies: The President demanded that countries dependent on Middle Eastern oil—specifically those that refused to join the war—must take the lead in protecting the Strait of Hormuz.
      • Direct Message: He suggested allies "build up some delayed courage" and "just take" the strait themselves, as the U.S. military has already done the "hard part."

Diplomatic and Domestic Context

  • NATO Tensions: Before the speech, Trump reportedly threatened to exit NATO due to allies' refusal to join the war effort. While legally difficult, analysts note he could severely limit U.S. participation via executive order.
  • Public Opinion: New polling indicates 60% of Americans disapprove of the war, and 67% believe the administration lacks a clear plan to resolve the conflict.
  • Negotiations vs. Escalation: Reporters noted a contradiction in Trump's rhetoric: he claimed Iran is "begging" for a ceasefire while Iranian state media remains defiant and the Strait of Hormuz remains closed.

NASA Achievement: Artemis II

  • Lunar Milestone: The briefing coincided with the successful launch of Artemis II, the first crewed mission to the moon in over 50 years.
  • Mission Details: The crew (Wiseman, Glover, Koch, and Hansen) is on a 10-day mission to orbit the moon. This serves as a precursor to establishing a permanent lunar base and eventually reaching Mars.

"I listened very carefully... there was nothing new in that speech... it was almost an afterthought when he talked about the negotiations with the Iranians." — Jonathan Karl, ABC News Chief Washington Correspondent

LIVE: Trump addresses the nation on the Iran war | NBC News

NBC News(11.9M) ·51:06 ·107.4K views · 2026-04-02
Donald Trump (President of the United States)
President Trump declared a tactical military victory over Iran following one month of "Operation Epic Fury," claiming the regime’s navy and air force are destroyed, though he extended the expected timeline for completion by another two to three weeks.
TL;DR President Trump declared a tactical military victory over Iran following one month of "Operation Epic Fury," claiming the regime’s navy and air force are destroyed, though he extended the expected timeline for completion by another two to three weeks. Despite the...

TL;DR

President Trump declared a tactical military victory over Iran following one month of "Operation Epic Fury," claiming the regime’s navy and air force are destroyed, though he extended the expected timeline for completion by another two to three weeks. Despite the President’s claims of a "new, more reasonable" Iranian regime and a pending return to low energy prices, analysts note that the Strait of Hormuz remains restricted and global oil markets reacted to the speech with price increases.

Military Status and "Operation Epic Fury"

  • Tactical Successes: President Trump stated that after four weeks of conflict, the Iranian navy has been "absolutely destroyed," their air force is in ruins, and the Islamic Revolutionary Guard Corps (IRGC) has been decimated.
      • Nuclear Infrastructure: The President highlighted "Operation Midnight Hammer," involving B-2 bombers that allegedly obliterated Iran’s primary nuclear facilities.
      • Casualties: The President confirmed that 13 American service members have been killed in the conflict to date.
  • Strategic Perspective: NBC News military analyst Col. Steve Warren clarified that while the U.S. has achieved "tactical military victories" (sinking ships, degrading ballistic missiles), it is much harder to claim a "strategic victory" regarding long-term regional stability.
  • Venezuela Reference: Trump claimed a secondary military success in Venezuela, describing the U.S. as "joint venture partners" in oil production following a "quick, lethal, violent" intervention.

Energy Independence and the Strait of Hormuz

  • The "Tehran Tollbooth": Correspondent Raf Sanchez reported that the Strait of Hormuz has slowed from 110 ships per day to roughly 5–10. Iran is reportedly forcing vessels into their waters and charging "tolls" of up to $2 million per passage.
  • U.S. Economic Strategy: Trump emphasized "drill baby drill" policies, asserting that the U.S. is now the top producer of oil and gas globally and is "totally independent" of Middle Eastern energy.
      • Allied Responsibility: The President argued the U.S. has no domestic need for the Strait of Hormuz and suggested that countries dependent on that oil must "take the lead" in protecting and reopening the passage.
  • Market Reaction: Despite Trump’s assurance that gas prices will drop, Brent crude oil prices jumped by $4 per barrel during his 20-minute address, reflecting market skepticism regarding a swift resolution.

Diplomacy and the "New Regime" Claims

  • Regime Change Status: Trump claimed that a "new group" is in power in Tehran following the deaths of original leaders, describing them as "less radical."
      • Expert Skepticism: NBC analysts noted there is "no evidence" of a truly new regime, pointing out that the son of the previous leader is in power and the underlying ideology remains unchanged.
  • Diplomatic Overlooks: Iranian President Masoud Pezeshkian released a 1,000-word conciliatory letter in English ahead of the speech. However, experts noted Pezeshkian lacks real power in the Iranian system, especially after the death of Supreme Leader Ayatollah Ali Khamenei.
  • Negotiation Track: While Trump mentioned ongoing discussions, he threatened to hit Iran’s electric generating plants "simultaneously" if a deal is not reached within the next 14 to 21 days.

Domestic Context and Artemis 2

  • Space Achievement: The President opened his address by congratulating NASA on the successful launch of Artemis 2, noting the four astronauts will travel further than any humans in history.
  • Inflation Discrepancy: Trump claimed there is "no inflation" in the U.S.; however, NBC’s Brian Cheung corrected the record, noting government data shows prices rose 2.4% on a yearly basis.
  • Public Opinion: Sources indicated the war is increasingly unpopular, with a majority of Americans disapproving of the military action as national gas prices exceed $4 per gallon.

Notable Quotes

"Never in the history of warfare has an enemy suffered such clear and devastating large-scale losses in a matter of weeks. Our enemies are losing and America... is winning and now winning bigger than ever before." — President Donald Trump
"If we define victory as accomplishing the military objectives that were initially laid out... it is a tactical military victory. Now, military objectives have to feed into a broader strategy... it would be a lot harder to say that there’s been a strategic victory tonight." — Colonel Steve Warren, NBC News Military Analyst

President Trump Addresses the Nation on Iran War

C-SPAN(1.8M) ·76:05 ·505.8K views · 2026-04-02
Donald Trump (President of the United States)
One month into "Operation Epic Fury," President Trump declared the near-total destruction of Iran’s military infrastructure and leadership, framing the conflict as a necessary "America First" action to permanently eliminate Iran’s nuclear ambitions and "conventional shield" of missiles and drones.
TL;DR One month into "Operation Epic Fury," President Trump declared the near-total destruction of Iran’s military infrastructure and leadership, framing the conflict as a necessary "America First" action to permanently eliminate Iran’s nuclear ambitions and "conventional...

TL;DR

One month into "Operation Epic Fury," President Trump declared the near-total destruction of Iran’s military infrastructure and leadership, framing the conflict as a necessary "America First" action to permanently eliminate Iran’s nuclear ambitions and "conventional shield" of missiles and drones.

Military Progress and "Operation Epic Fury"

  • Status of Forces: President Trump reported that after 32 days of conflict, Iran’s navy is "gone," its air force is in ruins, and the command structure of the Islamic Revolutionary Guard Corps (IRGC) has been decimated.
  • Targeting Leadership: The President stated that most of the regime's original leaders are now dead, leading to a "less radical" provisional government.
  • Operation Midnight Hammer: Trump highlighted a previous June strike where B-2 bombers "totally obliterated" key nuclear facilities to prevent the regime from reaching "weapons-grade" enrichment.
  • Conventional Shield: Secretary of State Marco Rubio emphasized that the primary goal was destroying Iran’s massive stockpile of drones and missiles, which functioned as a shield to protect their nuclear program from international interference.

Energy Independence and the Global Economy

  • Oil Production: Trump asserted that the U.S. is now the #1 producer of oil and gas globally, producing more than Saudi Arabia and Russia combined through "drill, baby, drill" policies.
  • Venezuela Partnership: The President claimed the U.S. military took control of Venezuela in a "quick, lethal" operation, turning the country into a "joint venture partner" to secure the world's second-largest oil reserves.
  • Strait of Hormuz:
      • U.S. Stance: Trump argued the U.S. is no longer dependent on the Strait for energy and suggested other nations must "build up some delayed courage" to protect their own shipping lanes.
      • Economic Outlook: Despite a short-term spike in gas prices and market volatility, Trump predicted a "roaring" economic recovery once the conflict concludes and the Strait "opens up naturally."

Geopolitical Strategy and NATO

  • The "Axis of Aggressors": Matthew Kroenig (Atlantic Council) identified a dangerous "World War III" style interlinkage between China, Russia, Iran, and North Korea, noting that China remains the most capable adversary the U.S. has ever faced.
  • NATO Friction: Trump expressed frustration with European allies for their reluctance to support Middle Eastern operations. While reports suggested a potential U.S. withdrawal from NATO, Kroenig noted the alliance remains a major asset and highlighted Secretary General Mark Rutte’s upcoming "Trump whisperer" visit to Washington.
  • Regional Allies: The administration reaffirmed strong support for Israel, Saudi Arabia, Qatar, the UAE, Kuwait, and Bahrain as key partners in the "decapitation" of the Iranian threat.

Domestic and International Reaction

  • Supportive Views: Callers praised Trump’s "peace through strength" approach and his "proactive" defense of American interests, with some students viewing the administration as securing the future for the next generation.
  • Critical Opposition:
      • Legal Concerns: Critics and Democratic leaders (e.g., Hakeem Jeffries, Chris Van Hollen) labeled the war "reckless," "unmoored," and a "war of choice" conducted without a formal declaration from Congress.
      • Israel Influence: Several independent and Republican callers questioned if the U.S. was acting as a "proxy for Israel" and expressed disappointment over the shift away from a "no new wars" campaign promise.
      • Humanitarian/Economic Impact: Callers raised concerns over the bombing of civilian infrastructure and the disconnect between the President’s "strong economy" rhetoric and the reality of rising costs at home.
"Never in the history of warfare has an enemy suffered such clear and devastating large-scale losses in a matter of weeks... We have all the cards, they have none." — President Donald Trump
"To the surprise of many, Trump is emerging as one of the most prolific deposer of despots... this long list of rogue states that we worried about in the 1990s and 2000s is becoming a short list." — Matthew Kroenig, Atlantic Council

Well, let me explain. Iran wants to have nuclear weapons. Of that, there is zero doubt. If what they truly wanted, which is what they claim, is nuclear energy, well they could have nuclear energy like all the other countries in the world have it, and that is you import the fuel and you build reactors above ground. That's not what Iran has done. They build their reactors and their facilities deep in mountains away from the public glare, and they want to enrich that material. The same equipment that they could use to enrich material for energy, they could use to quickly enrich it to weapons grade. So it is clear that they've been offered every opportunity to have a nuclear program that allows them to have energy, not weapons, and every single time they have turned it down. But why the attack now? Well, what was Iran trying to do? Iran was trying to build a conventional shield. In essence, have so many missiles, have so many drones that no one could attack them, and they were well on their way. We were on the verge of an Iran that had so many missiles and so many drones that no one could do anything about their nuclear weapons program in the future. That was an intolerable risk. Under no circumstances can a country run by radical Shia clerics with an apocalyptic vision of the future ever possess nuclear weapons. And under no circumstances can they be allowed to hide and protect that program and their ambitions behind a shield of missiles and drones that no one can do anything about. This was our last best chance to eliminate that conventional threat, that conventional shield that they were trying to build, and the president made the right decision to wipe it out now. That is the goal of this operation: to destroy their conventional missiles and their drone program so they can't hide behind it and finally have to deal with the world seriously about never, ever having nuclear weapons. And that was Secretary of State Marco Rubio earlier today talking about the war in Iran. Well, I think there are bright spots and then there are other challenges. The bright spots are that Iran has been one of the major threats to the United States since 1979, and this war is seriously degrading Iran's capabilities. As the administration has pointed out many times, Iran's nuclear program, its missile program, its navy, its air force, and its drones have been severely degraded. And so almost whatever happens at this point, Iran is going to come out of this war much weaker than it was before, and less able to threaten the United States and its allies and partners. On the downside, Iran does have asymmetric ways to strike back, and we have seen that it's used that power to essentially shut down energy trade through the Strait of Hormuz and the Persian Gulf by attacking some commercial ships and threatening to attack others. And so this is really the dilemma the Trump administration is facing right now. On one hand, I think the president would like to declare victory because of the really substantial damage he's done to Iran's military capability, but it's difficult to do that while Iran is holding the world economy hostage through its threats to the Strait of Hormuz. Well, in a recent Wall Street Journal editorial you wrote, it's entitled "Twilight of the Rogue States," you wrote that attacking Iran now will help us leave behind the national security problems of the past. Yes, that's right. And you know, that's a piece that's kind of looked over the past 40 years or 30 years of U.S. foreign policy, because after the end of the Cold War, the Soviet threat had been addressed, but the major challenge then facing the United States was the threat from rogue states: Iraq, Iran, Libya, North Korea, Cuba, Venezuela, Syria, and so on. And I think often the conventional wisdom is that America's post-Cold War strategy has been a failure. The war in Iraq and Afghanistan didn't go as well as we would have liked. Yet when one takes a step back and looks at the big picture, this long list of rogue states that threatened us in the 1990s and 2000s has essentially been eliminated. Iraq is gone, Saddam Hussein is gone, Gaddafi in Libya is gone, Assad in Syria is gone. And so if Trump succeeds in his ambition, which I think is to... he's already removed Maduro in Venezuela, I think he'd like to remove the Islamic Republic in Tehran, and he and Rubio have talked about getting rid of the communists in Cuba. To the surprise of many, Trump is emerging as one of the most prolific deposers of despots. And so this long list of rogue states that we worried about in the 1990s and 2000s is becoming a short list, and indeed, maybe eliminated in the coming months. Mr. Kroenig, was this a war of necessity in your viewpoint? I think necessity is maybe not the right standard. The use of military force has always been a tool of international politics. A powerful country like the United States, that has 30 allies around the world and has interests in every world region, since World War II has used military force to secure its interest and to deal with threats from problematic countries like Iran. And Iran is a problematic country. It was very close to building nuclear weapons last summer. It has the largest stockpile of ballistic missiles in the Middle East. The State Department has declared it the world's leading state sponsor of terror. It's killed many Americans over the years and has plots right now to kill former senior U.S. officials. It's right now working to try to kill former Trump one administration officials. So this country's a serious threat. And so I think it was just prudent for the United States, spotting an opportunity like it did, to use military force to set back the capabilities of this adversary. And I used to work in the intelligence community, and intelligence analysts analyze threats according to intent—what does your adversary want to do?—but also capability—what can your adversary do? And I think a lot of the media attention recently has focused on intent—you know, will the new government in Tehran be just as hostile as the last one?—and that's an important consideration. But there's really no doubt that the new government in Tehran is going to be much less capable than they were just three weeks ago. And that is an important improvement in the security environment of the United States that I think is not getting enough attention. So this is an evil, evil and very threatening regime. One of the other things that the president has indicated he is going to talk about tonight is a critique of NATO and what he sees as lack of support in this war effort and a potential U.S. withdrawal from NATO. And then, also there have been issues over the years with our NATO allies spending enough and so on. But ultimately, this is a strong alliance. It all positioned us to get rid of a cancer that has long simmered. It's known as the nuclear Iran and they didn't know what was coming, they never imagined it. Because of the Trump administration's policies, we produce more oil and gas than Saudi Arabia and Russia combined. Think of that: Saudi Arabia and Russia combined. And that number will soon be substantially higher than that. There's no country like us anywhere in the world and we're in great shape for the future. We've beaten and completely decimated Iran. They are decimated, both militarily and economically and in every other way, and the countries of the world that do receive oil through the Hormuz Strait must take care of that passage. They must cherish it, they must grab it and cherish it. They can do it easily. We will be helpful, but they should take the lead in protecting the oil that they so desperately depend on. So to those countries that can't get fuel, many of which refused to get involved in the decapitation of Iran—we had to do it ourselves. I have a suggestion: number one, buy oil from the United States of America—we have plenty, we have so much; and number two, build up some delayed courage—should have done it before, should have done it with us as we asked—go to the strait and just take it, protect it, use it for yourselves. Iran has been essentially decimated, the hard part is done, so it should be easy. And in any event, when this conflict is over, the strait will open up naturally, it'll just open up naturally. They're going to want to be able to sell oil because that's all they have to try and rebuild. It will resume the flowing and the gas prices will rapidly come back down, and stock prices will rapidly go back up—they haven't come down very much, frankly. They came down a little bit, but they've had some very good days over the last couple of days. But we had to take that little journey to Iran to get rid of this horrible threat. With our historic tax cuts where people are just now talking about receiving larger refunds than they ever thought possible, they are getting so much more money than they thought—that's from the great big beautiful bill. Our economy is strong and improving by the day and it will soon be roaring back like never before. It will top the levels that it was a month ago. I've made clear from the beginning of Operation Epic Fury that we will continue until our objectives are fully achieved. Thanks to the progress we've made, I can say tonight that we are on track to complete all of America's military objectives shortly, very shortly. We are going to hit them extremely hard over the next two to three weeks. We're going to bring them back to the Stone Ages where they belong. In the meantime, discussions are ongoing. Regime change was not our goal—we never said regime change—but regime change has occurred because of all of their original leaders' deaths. They're all dead. The new group is less radical and much more reasonable. Yet if during this period of time no deal is made, we have our eyes on key targets. If there is no deal, we are going to hit each and every one of their electric-generating plants very hard and probably simultaneously. We have not hit their oil, even though that's the easiest target of all, because it would not give them even a small chance of survival or rebuilding. But we could hit it and it would be gone and there's not a thing they could do about it. They have no anti-aircraft equipment, and their radar is 100 percent annihilated. We are unstoppable as a military force. The nuclear sites that we obliterated with the B-2 bombers have been hit so hard that it would take months to get near the nuclear dust and we have it under intense satellite surveillance and control. If we see them make a move, even a move for it, we'll hit them with missiles very hard again. We have all the cards, they have none. It's very important that we keep this conflict in perspective. American involvement in World War I lasted one year, seven months and five days. World War II lasted for three years, eight months and 25 days. The Korean War lasted for three years, one month and two days. The Vietnam War lasted for 19 years, five months and 29 days. Iraq went on for eight years, eight months and 28 days. We are in this military operation, so powerful, so brilliant, against one of the most powerful countries, for 32 days, and the country has been eviscerated and essentially is really no longer a threat. They were the bully of the Middle East, but they're the bully no longer. This is a true investment in your children and your grandchildren's future. The whole world is watching and they can't believe the power, strength and brilliance. They just can't believe what they're seeing. They leave it to your imagination, but they can't believe what they're seeing: the brilliance of the United States military. Tonight every American can look forward to a day when we are finally free from the wickedness of Iranian aggression and the specter of nuclear blackmail. Because of the actions we have taken, we are on the cusp of ending Iran's sinister threat to America and the world. And I'll tell you, the world is watching, and when we do, once it's all over, the United States will be safer, stronger, more prosperous and greater than it has ever been before. May God bless the men and women of the United States Armed Forces and may God bless the United States of America. Thank you very much and good night. We want to get your reaction next about the president's speech and the war in Iran. 202 is the area code for all of our numbers: 748-8920 if you are a Republican, 748-8921 if you are a Democrat, and if you are neither of the above, 202-748-8922. You can see all the social media addresses at the bottom where you can continue the conversation or send us a comment as well. Rejoining us now is Matthew Kroenig of the Atlantic Council. He held positions in the defense and intelligence areas for George W. Bush, Barack Obama and for Donald Trump. What's your initial reaction to the president's speech, Mr. Kroenig? Well, not a lot of new information; repeated a lot of the points the administration has been making for several weeks about the threat that Iran poses to the United States and the world. There was a part of the speech talking about the military progress in terms of degrading Iran's capability. The president also repeated this point that if the European allies are concerned about the Strait of Hormuz, then they can come and help to secure the strait themselves. One thing that was new and interesting to me is he said that once the war ends, the Strait of Hormuz situation will resolve itself naturally, because Iran will have an incentive to open the strait to international commerce. I roughly agree with that point; it was put pretty simply in a short speech. So that was new, getting some insight into how the president thinks he might get the strait reopened after the conflict is over. So I'd say not a lot new but bringing together a lot of what has been said before. And of course it is powerful to do it in a primetime address from the president directly to the American people. So a lot of people who maybe weren't paying attention to the various press conferences and other things maybe were tuning in tonight, and so this was an opportunity for the president to present his comprehensive view of the war in Iran to the American people. Well, speaking of the Strait of Hormuz—and I... I don't know how far you can go in this—but it's about 21 miles wide. Iran is on the north or that half, and Oman is on the southern half, but there's only a small corridor that the ships can go through. Is that correct? That's right, and a large portion of the world's energy—oil and gas—every day transits through that strait, and so it is a choke point because it's so narrow and so easy for a country like Iran to threaten to close the strait by attacking ships that go through there. And so this is something that's been recognized for a long time. I worked on the Iran desk in the... during the Obama administration. This is something that we worried about—that if there was conflict with Iran, they could try to close the Strait of Hormuz. So I don't think this has caught anyone, or most experts anyway, by surprise, but it is right now the biggest challenge of this war and how do you get the strait reopened, how do you get energy transiting through the strait to fuel a global economy which relies on oil and gas from the Middle East? And the president did make a point about how the United States doesn't rely on energy from that region because it is energy independent now. He argued that Europe and others can buy energy from the United States, but the reality is it is a global market. So if there are supply disruptions in the Middle East, that has an effect on the prices and the economy for the entire world. He seemed to pull his punches when it came to NATO and the critique of NATO that we were hearing about this afternoon and the possible U.S. withdrawal from NATO. Well, if you go back to what I said before the speech, I said I think he's frustrated but I think at the end of the day, he does value NATO and the alliance will remain strong. So you're right, there are many people—so I guess I was right in my prediction. But you're right that there were many people who were worried today and, fortunately, the president didn't threaten to pull out of NATO or anything of the sort. And again, I think that's the right move. I know he's frustrated that the European allies aren't doing more to help, but on balance NATO is an important alliance for the United States, and so I think the president played it right in the speech tonight. And in fact, the Hill publication is reporting via X that NATO's Mark Rutte has scheduled a Washington trip as Trump reevaluates the alliance. Yeah, Secretary General Rutte has been very effective in the job and I think he understands that part of his job is keeping the United States engaged in Europe and engaged in NATO. And so, he's emerged as an important Trump whisperer, understanding Trump. You know, he was the one who played a role in getting Trump to pursue negotiations over his concerns with Greenland when we had tensions over that issue several weeks ago. And so yes, Rutte is coming to town, I think maybe next week, and I think that's on balance a good thing for the NATO Secretary General and the president of the United States to be working closely together. Have China and Russia been overly supportive of Iran during this war? No, and it's interesting because they are not formal treaty allies like the United States is with NATO, but they are close security partners. They've been working together in a number of ways that are troubling, including providing weapons and intelligence. And so many, I think, in the West worried if the United States were to do something like attack Iran, would Russia and China militarily intervene to help Iran? Would this lead to a direct superpower conflict? But, other than some critical statements and other than some reports that Russia is providing Iran with intelligence information, Russia and China really haven't done very much. And so, maybe a message to other rogue states out there: if you're planning on counting on Russia and China for your security, maybe you should think again. We also saw that they didn't come to the defense of Maduro in Venezuela after the U.S. military operation there. So, yes, they're condemning the United States but not really doing much practically to help Iran. What about the fear that China could use this as an excuse to go into Taiwan? Well, many people make that argument, but I don't buy it. And the main reason is China doesn't need an excuse. The Chinese Communist Party's official line is that Taiwan is already a part of China. It's a renegade province and so they're just going in to pacify it and reincorporate it into the Chinese mainland. And so that's been their story for decades. I don't think they're going to say, "Well, Trump did something in Iran, so now we can do something in Taiwan." Again, they already say that it's their right, essentially, to use military force in Taiwan. Matthew Kroenig, it seemed that the president was rather low-key or mute about the role of Israel. Was that on purpose, do you think? Well, that's a good point. He did talk early on about how they're working together. And, of course they have been working together, and early on in the conflict it was the United States going after the military targets, but it was Israel going after the leadership targets, including they're the ones credited with killing supreme leader Ayatollah Ali Khamenei. And so, yeah, good point—why did he not make a bigger deal out of that? You know, before the speech, you read the letter from Iran's president, that was full of, I'd call it anti-Semitic tropes about how, you know, Israel essentially tricked the United States into this war. And so maybe that's why the president played it the way he did: to make it clear that this is something that he wanted to do. And by the way, I guess I do think the Iranian president's letter doesn't really make much sense. President Trump is pretty strong-willed; hard to imagine that he's being led around by a small partner in the Middle East. So I think that was maybe the reason for that in the speech: to make it clear that this is something that President Trump has always thought important. He's always thought it was important to stop Iran from building nuclear weapons. And so this is an American action to protect Americans; it's not about what smaller partners in the region desire. Do you think his critique of the Iranian nuclear deal was fair? Well, it is a controversial issue; you've got people on both sides. I was a critic from the beginning for two reasons. One, when you make nuclear fuel, you can make nuclear fuel for a reactor for peaceful purposes, or you can make it for weapons; it's the exact same technology. And so U.S. policy has always been that other countries are not allowed to make the fuel. It's too dangerous and if you want fuel you can get it imported from the United States or Russia or other countries, but you can't make it yourself. And so that's a standard we've imposed on Mexico and United Arab Emirates and other partners. And that was originally our standard with Iran, but then, Iran wouldn't agree to that, and so with the nuclear deal, we relaxed our traditional standards and said, "Okay, Iran, you can enrich uranium. We will let you make fuel that you could use for nuclear weapons," potentially. And also, what many people don't understand is the nuclear deal was only temporary; the limits began to expire over time. And so I do think that over time it would have allowed Iran to build such a vast nuclear-fuel-making capability that it would have been very hard in practice to stop them from building nuclear weapons. So, you know... it's a political speech, and so the president maybe overplayed how terrible it was, but I do agree that I wouldn't have signed up for that deal. President Trump Delivers an Address to the Nation, Apr. 1, 2026

The White House(3.0M) ·28:30 ·805.0K views · 2026-04-02
Donald Trump (President of the United States)
One month into "Operation Epic Fury," President Trump announced the near-total decimation of Iran’s military and nuclear infrastructure, while confirming a strategic shift toward energy independence fueled by a recent military takeover of Venezuela.
TL;DR One month into "Operation Epic Fury," President Trump announced the near-total decimation of Iran’s military and nuclear infrastructure, while confirming a strategic shift toward energy independence fueled by a recent military takeover of Venezuela. Status of Hostilities:...

TL;DR

One month into "Operation Epic Fury," President Trump announced the near-total decimation of Iran’s military and nuclear infrastructure, while confirming a strategic shift toward energy independence fueled by a recent military takeover of Venezuela.

Operation Epic Fury: Military Progress in Iran

  • Status of Hostilities: Following 32 days of combat, the President reported that Iran's navy is "absolutely destroyed," its air force is in ruins, and the command structure of the Islamic Revolutionary Guard Corps (IRGC) has been decimated.
  • Nuclear Neutralization: Operation "Midnight Hammer" utilized B-2 bombers to obliterate key nuclear facilities. The administration is maintaining intense satellite surveillance to prevent any attempts at rebuilding.
  • Strategic Objectives:
      • Primary Goal: To permanently deny Iran nuclear weapons and dismantle their long-range ballistic missile program.
      • Leadership Impact: While "regime change" was not an explicit goal, the President stated it has effectively occurred because most original Iranian leaders are now dead.
  • Future Escalation: If no diplomatic agreement is reached shortly, the U.S. plans to target Iran’s electric generating plants and potentially its oil infrastructure, which has been spared thus far to allow for potential rebuilding.

Energy Independence and the Venezuela Intervention

  • Venezuelan "Joint Venture": The President highlighted a recent military operation to take over Venezuela, describing the hit as "quick, lethal, and violent." The U.S. and Venezuela are now acting as partners in the production of oil and gas.
  • Energy Production: The U.S. currently produces more oil and gas than Saudi Arabia and Russia combined.
      • Strategic Reserve: Venezuela holds the second-largest reserves on Earth after the United States.
  • The Strait of Hormuz: The President asserted that the U.S. no longer needs oil from the Middle East. He advised other nations dependent on the Strait to take the lead in protecting their own shipping lanes, suggesting they should instead "buy oil from the United States."

Economic Performance and Domestic Impact

  • Market Strength: Despite short-term gasoline price increases caused by Iranian attacks on commercial tankers, the President reported 53 all-time stock market highs within the last year.
  • Capital Inflow: Over $18 trillion in investments have entered the U.S. in the past year, which the administration credits with positioning the country to confront the Iranian threat.
  • Fiscal Policy: Mention was made of "historic tax cuts" leading to larger-than-expected refunds for American citizens.

Space Exploration and Historical Context

  • Artemis 2 Launch: The President opened the address by celebrating the successful launch of NASA's Artemis 2 mission.
      • Mission Scope: Four astronauts are traveling further than any manned rocket in history, passing substantially beyond the moon before returning.
  • Military Efficiency: To emphasize the speed of current operations, the President compared the 32-day conflict in Iran to past wars:
      • World War II: 3 years, 8 months.
      • Vietnam War: Over 19 years.
      • Iraq War: Over 8 years.
      • Operation Epic Fury: 32 days to "eviscerate" a primary regional threat.
"Never in the history of warfare has an enemy suffered such clear and devastating large-scale losses in a matter of weeks. Our enemies are losing and America... is winning and now winning bigger than ever before." — President Donald J. Trump
"We don’t need their oil. We don’t need anything they have, but we’re there to help our allies." — President Donald J. Trump
"We are going to hit them extremely hard over the next two to three weeks. We are going to bring them back to the Stone Ages where they belong." — President Donald J. Trump
Thank you very much. My fellow Americans, good evening. Let me begin by congratulating the team at NASA and our brave astronauts on the successful launch of Artemis 2. It was quite something. It will be traveling further than any manned rocket has ever flown and will go very substantially past the moon, go around it, and come back home from a distance that has never been done before. It's amazing. They are on the way and God bless them. These are brave people. We want to God bless those four unbelievable astronauts. As we speak this evening, it's been just one month since the United States military began Operation Epic Fury, targeting the world's number one state sponsor of terror, Iran. In these past four weeks, our armed forces have delivered swift, decisive, overwhelming victories on the battlefield. Victories like few people have ever seen before. Tonight, Iran's navy is gone, their air force is in ruins, and their leaders—most of them the terrorist regime they led—are now dead. Their command and control of the Islamic Revolutionary Guard Corps is being decimated as we speak. Their ability to launch missiles and drones is dramatically curtailed, and their weapons factories and rocket launchers are being blown to pieces, with very few of them left. Never in the history of warfare has an enemy suffered such clear and devastating large-scale losses in a matter of weeks. Our enemies are losing and America, as it has been for five years under my presidency, is winning and now winning bigger than ever before. Before discussing this current situation, I also want to thank our troops for the masterful job they did in taking the country of Venezuela in a matter of minutes. That hit was quick, lethal, violent, and respected by everyone all over the world. After rebuilding our military during my first term, we have by far the strongest military anywhere in the world. And now we're working along with Venezuela and are, in a true sense, joint venture partners. We're getting along incredibly well in the production and sale of massive amounts of oil and gas, the second largest reserves on Earth after the United States of America. We're now totally independent of the Middle East and yet we are there to help. We don't have to be there. We don't need their oil. We don't need anything they have, but we're there to help our allies. Tonight I want to provide an update on the tremendous progress our warriors have made in Iran and discuss why Operation Epic Fury is necessary for the safety of America and the security of the free world. From the very first day I announced my campaign for president in 2015, I have vowed that I would never allow Iran to have a nuclear weapon. This fanatical regime has been chanting "Death to America," "Death to Israel" for 47 years. Their proxies were behind the murder of 241 Americans in the Marine barracks bombing in Beirut and the slaughter of hundreds of our service members with roadside bombs. They were involved in the attack on the USS Cole and they carried out countless other heinous acts including the blood—just horrible, bloody atrocities of October 7th in Israel, something that most people have never seen anything like it. This murderous regime also recently killed 45,000 of their own people who were protesting in Iran. 45,000 dead. For these terrorists to have nuclear weapons would be an intolerable threat. The most violent and thuggish regime on Earth would be free to carry out their campaigns of terror, coercion, conquest, and mass murder from behind a nuclear shield. I will never let that happen and neither should any of our past presidents. This situation has been going on for 47 years and should have been handled long before I arrived in office. I did many things during my two terms in office to stop the quest for nuclear weapons by Iran. First, and perhaps most importantly, I killed General Qassem Soleimani in my first term. He was an evil genius, a brilliant person, but a horrible human being—the father of the roadside bomb. And what he did was just horrible. Iran would have been, perhaps, in a far better, stronger position had he lived. We would have had probably a different conversation tonight. But you know what? We'd still be winning and winning big. And then, very importantly, I terminated Barack Hussein Obama's Iran nuclear deal, a disaster. Obama gave them 1.7 billion dollars in cash—green, green cash. He took it out of banks from Virginia, D.C., and Maryland. All the cash they had. He flew it by airplane in an attempt to buy their respect and loyalty, but it didn't work. They laughed at our president and went on with their mission to have a nuclear bomb. His Iran deal would have led to a colossal arsenal of massive nuclear weapons for Iran, and they would have had them years ago and they would have used them. It would have been a different world. There would have been no Middle East and no Israel right now, in my opinion and the opinion of a lot of great experts, had I not terminated that terrible deal that I was so honored to do, so proud to do. It was so bad right from the beginning. Essentially, I did what no other president was willing to do. They made mistakes and I am correcting them. My first preference was always the path of diplomacy, yet the regime continued their relentless quest for nuclear weapons and rejected every attempt at an agreement. For this reason, in June, I ordered a strike on Iran's key nuclear facilities in Operation Midnight Hammer. Nobody's ever seen anything like it. Those beautiful B-2 bombers performed magnificently. We totally obliterated those nuclear sites. The regime then sought to rebuild their nuclear program at a totally different location, making clear they had no intention of abandoning their pursuit of nuclear weapons. They were also rapidly building a vast stockpile of conventional ballistic missiles and would soon have had missiles that could reach the American homeland, Europe, and virtually any other place on Earth. Iran's strategy was so obvious. They wanted to produce as many missiles as possible and they did, with the longest range possible, and they had some weapons that nobody believed they had. We just learned that out. We took them out and we took them all out so that no one would really dare stop them in their race for a nuclear bomb—a nuclear weapon like nobody's ever seen before. They were right at the doorstep. For years everyone has said that Iran cannot have nuclear weapons, but in the end those are just words if you're not willing to take action when the time comes. As I stated in my announcement of Operation Epic Fury, our objectives are very simple and clear. We are systematically dismantling the regime's ability to threaten America or project power outside of their borders. That means eliminating Iran's navy, which is now absolutely destroyed, hurting their air force and their missile program at levels never seen before, and annihilating their defense industrial base. We've done all of it. Their navy is gone, their air force is gone, and their missiles are just about used up or beaten. Taken together, these actions will cripple Iran's military, crush their ability to support terrorist proxies, and deny them the ability to build a nuclear bomb. Our armed forces have been extraordinary. There's never been anything like it militarily. Everyone is talking about it, and tonight I'm pleased to say that these core strategic objectives are nearing completion. As we celebrate this progress, we think especially of the 13 American warriors who have laid down their lives in this fight to prevent our children from ever having to face a nuclear Iran. Twice this past month I have traveled to Dover Air Force Base, and it's been something. I wanted to be with those heroes as they return to American soil and I was with them and their families—their parents, their wives, the husbands. We salute them and now we must honor them by completing the mission for which they gave their lives. Every single one of the people, their loved ones, said, "Please sir, please finish the job." Every one of them. And we are going to finish the job and we're going to finish it very fast. We're getting very close. I want to thank our allies in the Middle East: Israel, Saudi Arabia, Qatar, the UAE, Kuwait, and Bahrain. They've been great and we will not let them get hurt or fail in any way, shape, or form. Many Americans have been concerned to see the recent rise in gasoline prices here at home. This short-term increase has been entirely the result of the Iranian regime launching deranged terror attacks against commercial oil tankers and neighboring countries that have nothing to do with the conflict. This is yet more proof that Iran can never be trusted with nuclear weapons. They will use them and they will use them quickly. It would lead to decades of extortion, economic pain, and instability worse than we can ever imagine. The United States has never been better prepared economically to confront this threat. You all know that. We built the strongest economy in history. We're going through it right now, the strongest in history. In one year we've taken a dead and crippled country—I hate to say that, but we were a dead and crippled country after the last administration—and made it the hottest country anywhere in the world by far. We have no inflation, record-setting investments coming into the United States of over 18 trillion dollars, and the highest stock market ever with 53 all-time record highs in just one year. It all positioned us to get rid of a cancer that has long simmered. It's known as the nuclear Iran, and they didn't know what was coming. They've never imagined it. Remember because of our "drill baby drill" program, America has plenty of gas; we have so much gas. Under my leadership, we are the number one producer of oil and gas on the planet, without even discussing the millions of barrels that we're getting from Venezuela. Because of the Trump administration's policies, we produce more oil and gas than Saudi Arabia and Russia combined. Think of that, Saudi Arabia and Russia combined, and that number will soon be substantially higher than that. There's no country like us anywhere in the world and we're in great shape for the future. The United States imports almost no oil through the Hormuz Strait and won't be taking any in the future. We don't need it. We haven't needed it and we don't need it. We've beaten and completely decimated Iran. They are decimated both militarily and economically and in every other way. And the countries of the world that do receive oil through the Hormuz Strait must take care of that passage. They must cherish it. They must grab it and cherish it. They can do it easily. We will be helpful, but they should take the lead in protecting the oil that they so desperately depend on. So to those countries that can't get fuel, many of which refused to get involved in the decapitation of Iran, we had to do it ourselves. I have a suggestion: number one, buy oil from the United States of America. We have plenty, we have so much. And number two, build up some delayed courage—should've done it before, should've done it with us as we asked—go to the strait and just take it, protect it, use it for yourselves. Iran has been essentially decimated. The hard part is done, so it should be easy. And in any event, when this conflict is over, the strait will open up naturally. It'll just open up naturally. They're going to want to be able to sell oil because that's all they have to try and rebuild. It will resume flowing and the gas prices will rapidly come back down. Stock prices will rapidly go back up. They haven't come down very much frankly. They came down a little bit but they've had some very good days over the last couple of days. We've done actually much better than I thought. But we had to take that little journey to Iran to get rid of this horrible threat. With our historic tax cuts, where people are just now talking about receiving larger refunds than they ever thought possible, they are getting so much more money than they thought. That's from the great big beautiful bill. Our economy is strong and improving by the day and it will soon be roaring back like never before. It will top the levels that it was a month ago. I've made clear from the beginning of Operation Epic Fury that we will continue until our objectives are fully achieved. Thanks to the progress we've made, I can say tonight that we are on track to complete all of America's military objectives shortly, very shortly. We are going to hit them extremely hard over the next two to three weeks. We are going to bring them back to the Stone Ages where they belong. In the meantime, discussions are ongoing. Regime change was not our goal—we never said regime change—but regime change has occurred because of all of their original leaders' deaths. They're all dead. The new group is less radical and much more reasonable. Yet if during this period of time no deal is made, we have our eyes on key targets. If there is no deal, we are going to hit each and every one of their electric generating plants very hard and probably simultaneously. We have not hit their oil, even though that's the easiest target of all, because it would not give them even a small chance of survival or rebuilding. But we could hit it and it would be gone and there's not a thing they could do about it. They have no anti-aircraft equipment and their radar is 100 percent annihilated. We are unstoppable as a military force. The nuclear sites that we obliterated with the B-2 bombers have been hit so hard that it would take months to get near the nuclear dust, and we have it under intense satellite surveillance and control. If we see them make a move, even a move for it, we'll hit them with missiles very hard again. We have all the cards and they have none. It's very important that we keep this conflict in perspective. American involvement in World War I lasted one year, seven months, and five days. World War II lasted for three years, eight months, and 25 days. The Korean War lasted for three years, one month, and two days. The Vietnam War lasted for 19 years, five months, and 29 days. Iraq went on for eight years, eight months, and 28 days. We are in this military operation—so powerful, so brilliant—against one of the most powerful countries for 32 days, and the country has been eviscerated and essentially is really no longer a threat. They were the bully of the Middle East, but they're the bully no longer. This is a true investment in your children and your grandchildren's future. The whole world is watching and they can't believe the power, strength, and brilliance. They just can't believe what they're seeing. They leave it to your imagination, but they can't believe what they're seeing: the brilliance of the United States military. Tonight every American can look forward to a day when we are finally free from the wickedness of Iranian aggression and the specter of nuclear blackmail. Because of the actions we have taken, we are on the cusp of ending Iran's sinister threat to America and the world. And I'll tell you, the world is watching. When it's all over, the United States will be safer, stronger, more prosperous, and greater than it has ever been before. May God bless the men and women of the United States Armed Forces, and may God bless the United States of America. Thank you very much and goodnight.

President Trump speaks to the nation on Iran at the White House — 4/1/2026

CNBC Television(3.4M) ·20:01 ·400.5K views · 2026-04-02
Donald Trump (President of the United States)

TL;DR President Trump announced that "Operation Epic Fury" has effectively decimated Iran’s military and nuclear capabilities within 32 days, shifting the U.S. focus toward a final two-to-three-week campaign to permanently eliminate the Iranian threat while leveraging newly...

TL;DR

President Trump announced that "Operation Epic Fury" has effectively decimated Iran’s military and nuclear capabilities within 32 days, shifting the U.S. focus toward a final two-to-three-week campaign to permanently eliminate the Iranian threat while leveraging newly secured energy independence.

Military Progress and "Operation Epic Fury"

  • Operational Status: The U.S. military has been engaged in Iran for 32 days, achieving what the President described as "overwhelming victories" that have eviscerated the country’s defense capabilities.
      • Asset Destruction: Iran’s navy has been "absolutely destroyed," its air force is in ruins, and the Islamic Revolutionary Guard Corps (IRGC) command structure is decimated.
      • Nuclear Facilities: Following "Operation Midnight Hammer" in June, B-2 bombers reportedly obliterated key nuclear sites; these locations remain under intense satellite surveillance.
      • Leadership Status: While the President stated "regime change was not our goal," he noted that it has occurred by default because most of Iran’s original leaders are now dead.
  • Historical Comparison: The President contrasted the 32-day duration of this conflict with the years-long durations of World War II, the Vietnam War, and the Iraq War.

Energy Independence and Regional Shifts

  • Venezuelan Integration: The President highlighted the recent military takeover of Venezuela, describing it as "quick, lethal, and violent."
      • Joint Venture: The U.S. is now "joint venture partners" with Venezuela, utilizing the world’s second-largest oil and gas reserves.
  • Energy Production: The U.S. currently produces more oil and gas than Saudi Arabia and Russia combined.
  • Strait of Hormuz: The U.S. no longer imports oil through the Strait and has "no need" for Middle Eastern energy.
      • International Responsibility: The President suggested that other nations dependent on the Strait must "build up some delayed courage" and take the lead in protecting that passage themselves.

Strategic Objectives and Deterrence

  • Nuclear Red Line: A central pillar of the briefing was the vow to never allow Iran to possess a nuclear weapon, citing 47 years of Iranian aggression and the "bloody atrocities" of October 7th in Israel.
  • Past Policy Critiques: The President reiterated his termination of the Obama-era nuclear deal, criticizing the $1.7 billion cash payment and the previous administration's "mistakes."
  • Allied Support: Continued support was pledged for Middle Eastern allies, including Israel, Saudi Arabia, Qatar, the UAE, Kuwait, and Bahrain.
  • Casualties: The President honored 13 American "warriors" who died during the month-long operation.

Economic Outlook and Final Ultimatum

  • Domestic Economy: Despite short-term gasoline price increases caused by Iranian attacks on tankers, the President cited a record-setting stock market with 53 all-time highs in one year and $18 trillion in new investments.
  • Final Timeline: The U.S. intends to "hit them extremely hard" over the next two to three weeks to achieve all military objectives.
  • Targeting Strategy:
      • Infrastructure: If no diplomatic deal is reached, the U.S. will target all of Iran's electric generating plants simultaneously.
      • Oil Assets: The U.S. has intentionally avoided hitting Iranian oil fields to allow the country a chance to rebuild eventually, though they remain "the easiest target of all."
  • Space Achievement: The briefing opened with a commendation of the Artemis 2 mission, noting the astronauts are traveling further than any manned rocket in history.

Thank you very much. My fellow Americans, good evening. Let me begin by congratulating the team at NASA and our brave astronauts on the successful launch of Artemis 2. It was quite something. It will be traveling further than any manned rocket has ever flown and will very substantially pass the moon, go around it, and come back home from a distance that has never been done before. It's amazing. They are on the way and God bless them; these are brave people. We want to God bless those four unbelievable astronauts. As we speak this evening, it's been just one month since the United States military began Operation Epic Fury, targeting the world's number one state sponsor of terror, Iran. In these past four weeks, our armed forces have delivered swift, decisive, overwhelming victories on the battlefield. Victories like few people have ever seen before. Tonight, Iran's navy is gone. Their air force is in ruins. Their leaders—most of them—and the terrorist regime they led are now dead. Their command and control of the Islamic Revolutionary Guard Corps is being decimated as we speak. Their ability to launch missiles and drones is dramatically curtailed and their weapons factories and rocket launchers are being blown to pieces, with very few of them left. Never in the history of warfare has an enemy suffered such clear and devastating large-scale losses in a matter of weeks. Our enemies are losing and America, as it has been for five years under my presidency, is winning and now winning bigger than ever before. Before discussing this current situation, I also want to thank our troops for the masterful job they did in taking the country of Venezuela in a matter of minutes. That hit was quick, lethal, violent, and respected by everyone all over the world. After rebuilding our military during my first term, we have by far the strongest military anywhere in the world and now we're working along with Venezuela. In a true sense, we are joint venture partners. We're getting along incredibly well in the production and sale of massive amounts of oil and gas, the second largest reserves on Earth after the United States of America. We're now totally independent of the Middle East and yet we are there to help. We don't have to be there, we don't need their oil, we don't need anything they have, but we're there to help our allies. Tonight, I want to provide an update on the tremendous progress our warriors have made in Iran and discuss why Operation Epic Fury is necessary for the safety of America and the security of the free world. From the very first day I announced my campaign for president in 2015, I have vowed that I would never allow Iran to have a nuclear weapon. This fanatical regime has been chanting "Death to America" and "Death to Israel" for 47 years. Their proxies were behind the murder of 241 Americans in the Marine barracks bombing in Beirut and the slaughter of hundreds of our service members with roadside bombs. There would have been no Middle East and no Israel right now, in my opinion and the opinion of a lot of great experts, had I not terminated that terrible deal. We totally obliterated those nuclear sites. The regime then sought to rebuild their nuclear program at a totally different location, making clear they had no intention of abandoning their pursuit of nuclear weapons. They were also rapidly building a vast stockpile of conventional ballistic missiles and would soon have had missiles that could reach the American homeland, Europe, and virtually any other place on Earth. Iran's strategy was so obvious. They wanted to produce as many missiles as possible, and they did, with the longest range possible. Special Report: President Trump delivers update on war with Iran

NBC News(11.9M) ·22:40 ·127.2K views · 2026-04-02
Donald Trump (President of the United States)
President Trump declared that "Operation Epic Fury" has effectively decimated Iran's military capabilities in just 32 days, signaling a potential conclusion to the conflict within two to three weeks.
TL;DR President Trump declared that "Operation Epic Fury" has effectively decimated Iran's military capabilities in just 32 days, signaling a potential conclusion to the conflict within two to three weeks. However, the President issued a stern ultimatum: if a deal is not...

TL;DR

President Trump declared that "Operation Epic Fury" has effectively decimated Iran's military capabilities in just 32 days, signaling a potential conclusion to the conflict within two to three weeks. However, the President issued a stern ultimatum: if a deal is not reached, the U.S. will escalate strikes to target Iran’s civilian power grid.

Military Status and "Operation Epic Fury"

  • Current Progress: President Trump reported that after one month of military action, Iran’s navy is "gone," its air force is in ruins, and the Islamic Revolutionary Guard Corps (IRGC) command structure has been decimated.
  • Operational Timeline: The President stated the U.S. is on track to complete core strategic objectives "shortly," suggesting a window of two to three more weeks of high-intensity strikes.
  • Nuclear Neutralization: Trump claimed that earlier strikes under "Operation Midnight Hammer" (conducted in June) successfully obliterated Iran’s nuclear facilities, and the sites remain under intense satellite surveillance to prevent rebuilding.
  • U.S. Casualties: The President confirmed that 13 American service members have died during the operation to date.

Strategic Ultimatum and Regime Status

  • Targeting Infrastructure: Trump warned that if the Iranian leadership does not reach a deal, the U.S. will hit "each and every one" of Iran's electric generating plants simultaneously.
  • Regime Change Claims: The President asserted that "regime change has occurred" because the original leadership is dead.
      • Fact Check: NBC’s Tom Llamas and Hallie Jackson noted that while the former Ayatollah was killed, he was replaced by his son, and the Iranian President remains in power, making the "regime change" claim questionable.
  • Negotiation Disparity: While Trump mentioned ongoing discussions with a "more reasonable" new leadership, NBC’s Garrett Haake reported that Iranian officials deny any negotiations are taking place.

Energy Independence and Regional Dynamics

  • The Venezuela Precedent: Trump highlighted a "quick, lethal" military action in Venezuela earlier in his term, claiming the U.S. and Venezuela are now "joint venture partners" in oil production.
  • Strait of Hormuz: The President addressed the closure of the Strait of Hormuz, which has spiked global gas prices.
      • U.S. Stance: He stated the U.S. no longer needs Middle Eastern oil due to domestic production and the Venezuelan partnership.
      • Global Responsibility: Trump argued that countries dependent on the Strait must "take the lead" in protecting it themselves rather than relying on the U.S. military.
  • Domestic Impact: Despite Trump's claims of a "roaring" economy, NBC reporting highlighted that the war remains unpopular with a majority of Americans due to rising fuel costs.

Historical and Economic Context

  • Comparative Warfare: Trump contrasted the 32-day duration of Operation Epic Fury against longer historical conflicts like Vietnam (19+ years) and Iraq (8+ years) to emphasize military efficiency.
  • Economic Resilience: The President credited his "drill baby drill" policies and tax cuts for providing the economic buffer necessary to sustain a conflict without causing a domestic collapse.

***

Notable Quotes

"Never in the history of warfare has an enemy suffered such clear and devastating large-scale losses in a matter of weeks. Our enemies are losing and America... is winning and now winning bigger than ever before." — President Donald Trump
"We are going to hit them extremely hard over the next two to three weeks. We're going to bring them back to the Stone Ages where they belong." — President Donald Trump
"The President is addressing the nation about a war that is pretty unpopular, especially right now. Polling shows that a majority of Americans do not approve of this military action." — Hallie Jackson, Senior Washington Correspondent
"We have all the cards, they have none... This is a true investment in your children's and your grandchildren's future." — President Donald Trump

The Private Credit Reckoning is Coming: Executives Are Mistaking Luck For Genius | The Weekly Wrap

Steve Eisman(166.0K) ·20:30 ·78.9K views · 2026-04-02
Steve Eisman (Host, The Weekly Wrap)
Private credit executives are exhibiting the same systemic arrogance seen on Wall Street prior to the 2008 financial crisis, mistaking a 17-year absence of a credit cycle for personal genius while hiding significant risks through "data massaging.
TL;DR Private credit executives are exhibiting the same systemic arrogance seen on Wall Street prior to the 2008 financial crisis, mistaking a 17-year absence of a credit cycle for personal genius while hiding significant risks through "data massaging." The Iran War Variable:...

TL;DR

Private credit executives are exhibiting the same systemic arrogance seen on Wall Street prior to the 2008 financial crisis, mistaking a 17-year absence of a credit cycle for personal genius while hiding significant risks through "data massaging."

Geopolitical Volatility and Market Sentiment

  • The Iran War Variable: Steve Eisman identifies the war as the primary driver of market movement, noting that the S&P 500 and Nasdaq ended Q1 down 4.6% and 7.1% respectively, largely due to conflict-related fears.
  • Trump’s Strategy: Contradictory headlines are causing market whiplash. While the *Wall Street Journal* reported Trump might end the war without reopening the Strait of Hormuz, Trump’s own social media statements suggest a more aggressive stance, demanding other nations "go get your own oil."
  • Investment Difficulty: Eisman expresses skepticism that Trump would accept a closed Strait, as it would be viewed as a defeat, making current investment decisions difficult as the market "trades headlines."

The "Data Massaging" of Private Credit

  • Understated Software Exposure: A recent *Wall Street Journal* analysis suggests private credit funds are intentionally misclassifying loans to make software exposure appear smaller than it is (often labeling software companies as "Healthcare" or other sectors they serve).
  • Significant Discrepancies: Four major funds showed a marked difference between reported and actual software exposure:
      • Blue Owl Credit Income Fund: Reported 11.6%; Actual ~21%.
      • Blackstone (BCRED): Reported 25.7%; Actual ~33%.
      • Ares Capital Corp: Reported 23.8%; Actual ~30%.
      • Apollo Debt Solutions Fund: Reported 13.6%; Actual ~16%.
  • The AI Threat: If AI disrupts the software sector, these massive, opaque exposures could lead to "ugly" losses that bleed into banks, pension funds, and life insurance companies.

Psychological Herd Mentality in Hedge Funds

  • Counterintuitive Market Moves: Despite war and inflation—factors that usually drive gold prices up—gold has declined 10%.
  • Forced Liquidation: Eisman attributes this to "herd mentality" among major funds (Citadel, Millennium, etc.). These funds held similar trades betting on lower rates and higher gold. When interest rate bets went wrong, risk managers forced them to sell their gold positions to cover losses, driving the price down.

Structural Risks: Mistaking Luck for Genius

  • The "Lack of Cycle" Delusion: Eisman argues that because there hasn't been a significant credit cycle in 17 years, current lending executives have forgotten that the "cost of goods sold" in lending is future losses.
  • Arrogance Parallel to 2008: Just as GFC-era bankers mistook high leverage for genius, today’s private credit executives mistake a long period of low defaults for superior underwriting.
  • Opaqueness: Because these funds price their own loan portfolios (marking their own cards), the industry lacks the transparency required to maintain investor trust during a downturn.

Mailbag: GameStop and Fund Structures

  • GameStop (GME) Analysis: Eisman rejects the idea that GME is a "value stock." While the company has $2.2 billion in net cash, its core retail business is terminal. He views Michael Burry’s thesis—that GME could use cash for acquisitions—as a "pipe dream" with too many variables.
  • Private Funds vs. BDCs:
      • BDCs (e.g., OCSL): Publicly listed, regulated by the SEC, limited to 2:1 leverage, and must distribute 90% of income.
      • Private Vehicles (e.g., BCRED): Restricted to "qualified purchasers," they avoid SEC registration, face no leverage limits, and have no public reporting requirements, making them more attractive to managers seeking higher fees and less oversight.
